Five Brokers Associations Resolved Yesterday to Oppose New Telephone Regulations; Decided on Four Principles to Negotiate with the Company; And Called on All Industries to Act Together 93

According to the Industrial News Agency, the brokers' associations of the five exchanges in this city held a joint meeting at the joint association's headquarters at 4:00 PM yesterday to oppose the new telephone regulations. Attendees included Wu Xunxiang, Kuang Jian, and Shi Donglai from the yarn and cloth industry; Zhan Liansheng, Zhang Zhusun, and Gao Qiumei from the gold industry; Zhu Anfu and Qiu Lianggui from the securities industry; Xu Jianqi and Xue Chengzhang from the grain industry; and Yang Jingcheng, Zhu Jiansheng, Wang Zhongliang, and Zhang Songchun from the flour industry, and ten others. Wu Xunqing chaired the meeting, and Secretary Shao Xinru recorded the minutes. After the usual rituals, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that since the implementation of the new telephone regulations, which charge per pulse, only half a month has passed, and the losses to users have been unexpected. If this continues, it will be unbearable. The association had expressed its opposition to this proposal in March last year, but the telephone company disregarded public opinion and insisted on its own way. The association should make another statement in order to implement the original intention. Then, the following was discussed: This is not appropriate to telephone change ordering new chapter, press decides charges, increasing user burden, this association shall request restoration of the status quo from the authority. After the representatives of the various offices expressed their views successively, the result was to resolve the requirements principle, slightly divided into four points: (A) Request to increase the basic charge number, (B) Reduce additional charges, (C) Install a meter on the user's telephone, (D) Hope that the telephone company will save expenses in order to lighten the user's burden. The above methods, in addition to being directly communicated to the telephone company by the association, also call on users in all industries to act together, hoping to achieve the most recent victory. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned at about 6:00 PM.

Taxpayers' Association Requests Electricity Company to Return Improper Fines 95

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "To the Director, we have recently received a letter from Zhong Chunji Barber Shop, stating that, 'Regarding our electricity meter issue, we are extremely grateful that your association has forwarded a letter to the Public Works Department on March 2, urging the electricity company to negotiate reasonably. However, for the second installment, the company requires payment by approximately March 20, otherwise they will cut off the power supply. We believe the Public Works Department is the most impartial organization in the concession, safeguarding the citizens' rights. We hope that the improper fines we paid to the Shanghai Electric Power Company will be returned in full and impartially in the near future. Furthermore, we hope that not only will this be the case for us, but that other electricity users will no longer experience similar oppression. After this incident, we originally did not want to continue using electricity, but due to the nature of the barber business, which cannot operate without electricity, we have no choice but to temporarily endure the hardship. Your association is the voice of the Chinese taxpayers, and should not allow such pressure to be repeatedly applied to the taxpaying citizens.' Ministry of Industry Held Flour Inspection Team Meeting in Shanghai Yesterday 97

The Technical Research Committee for Commodity Inspection of the Ministry of Industry convened the first subgroup meeting yesterday (the 16th) at the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, which will continue until the 18th. Representatives from various commodity inspection bureaus attended, including Wu Jiazhen from Tianjin, Zhai Nianpu from Qingdao, Chen Zihui from Hankou, and Zhou Zhenjun and Jiang Gongchen from Shanghai. Wu Jiazhen, the standing committee member of the committee, chaired the meeting, with Chuan Tingxian recording. The chairman delivered the opening remarks, stating that the flour inspection plan was first discussed at the National Commodity Inspection Technical Conference in 1933, and then approved at the second meeting in Qingdao in 1934. It was officially launched by order of the Ministry at the end of 1934. Tianjin and Qingdao started in January 1935, followed by Shanghai in September 1935 and Hankou in March of this year. There were some difficulties in terms of standards, so this meeting was convened to discuss and resolve various issues to facilitate implementation. Next, Cai Wuji, the director of the Shanghai Bureau, delivered a speech, stating that although he was not a member of the committee, he welcomed the participants as the host. He took the opportunity of the meeting to raise several points for attention and improvement in the bureau for discussion. Finally, each bureau reported on the progress of the implementation, and the meeting adjourned. It was scheduled to continue the meeting today.

Third Phase of Railway Bonds: Collateralized Cash Loan from Shanghai Banking Syndicate, Zhang Gongquan to Continue Negotiations After Returning from Inspection, Loan to Be Used for Developing Railways in Southwest China 98

The Ministry of Railways, to construct trunk lines such as the Hunan-Guizhou, Sichuan-Guangxi lines and develop the Ping-Sui, Zheng-Tai, and Jiao-Ji railways, issued the third phase of railway bonds for 120 million yuan. The first portion of 40 million yuan was officially issued on March 1. Minister of Railways Zhang Gongquan came to Shanghai to negotiate with the banking sector regarding cash collateralization. A reporter from the New News Agency interviewed Huo Baoshu of the Bank of China yesterday morning, who said that Minister Zhang had contacted the Shanghai banking sector several times regarding the collateralization of the first 40 million yuan of the third phase of railway bonds. The amount of collateral and the interest rate and term are still to be negotiated after Minister Zhang returns to Shanghai from his inspection in the southwest. It is expected that there will be no major issues. It is reported that the majority of this collateralized loan will be used for developing railways such as the Guangdong-Hankou and Guangzhou-Kowloon railways.

Chinese Industrial Federation Convened Manufacturers to Discuss Protecting Small Industries, To Form Group to Seek Improvements 99

The Chinese Industrial Federation held a joint meeting of factory managers and owners at its premises on Hankou Road at 2 p.m. yesterday to discuss how to protect small industries. More than ten people attended, including Ren Zhiyuan of Hongda Rubber Factory, Tang Zhiyu of Shanghai First Foundry, Ji Guorong of China Machine-Made Shoe Factory, Wang Danqing of Hua'an Machine-Made Box Factory, Lu Xifan of Ping'an Fire Extinguisher Factory, Wu Chunfa of Tengxin Machine Factory, Wang Junhua of Junlong Iron Factory, Zhou Wencuan of Jinghua Machine Factory, Zhou Xiqiu of Qinzong Machine Factory, and Li Qingxiang of Huade Factory. Qian Chengxu chaired the meeting, stating that the purpose of the meeting was to discuss how to overcome the current difficulties amidst the economic recession for Chinese products and what steps to take to find a way out. After discussion, the meeting participants agreed that a group should be formed to study and explore technical aspects in order to improve production. Regarding financial issues, efforts should be made to economize and enrich the content of the products as a prerequisite, seek a way out of difficulties, and encourage investment and sponsorship from all sectors. It is reported that the group will use the Chinese Industrial Federation as its headquarters and hold an inaugural meeting regularly.

Rice and Wheat Grading Laboratory Begins Rice Grading, Expected to Be Completed in Six Months, Wheat Grading to Begin in the Second Half of the Year 100

The Rice and Wheat Grading Laboratory, jointly established by the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce, has been dispatching experts to various counties in Jiangsu to investigate rice varieties since its establishment in Shanghai last year. The investigation is now complete, with more than 600 rice samples collected. Grading has now begun and is expected to be completed in six months. After the grading is completed, it can be used as a reference for warehouses and rice merchants in various counties. It is also learned that the investigation of wheat varieties will begin in the second half of the year. The entire project is expected to be completed in three years.

Memorial Service for Mr. Wang Guangqi Held the Day Before Yesterday, Various Circles Raise Funds for the Wang Guangqi Scholarship 101

The memorial service for Mr. Wang Guangqi was held on time at 10:30 a.m. the day before yesterday (the 15th) in the auditorium of the National Conservatory of Music in the city center. More than 100 people attended, including Xu Weiman, Guo Butao, Zhu Mengzhou, Huang Boqiao, Shu Xincheng, Shen Yi, Zhu Gong, Tai Shuangqiu, Shen Benqiang, and students from the National Conservatory of Music. Shu Xincheng chaired the meeting, Huang Zhongsu was the master of ceremonies, and Wu Yizhou played mourning music. The chairman delivered the closing remarks, stating that Mr. Wang had studied in Germany for sixteen years and had never received any subsidies from the government or private sources. His daily life depended entirely on writing. His great spirit of perseverance was a model for modern youth. Then, Zuo Shunsheng reported on Mr. Wang's life and mentioned that Mr. Wang was the founder of the Young China Association, which was based on the spirit of science and social activity to create a Young China. He said that Mr. Wang's words and deeds throughout his life were worthy of this title. Originally, Xiao Youmei, the president of the National Conservatory of Music, was scheduled to give a speech, but he was unable to do so due to illness and was replaced by Huang Zi, a professor at the school. His speech mainly introduced Mr. Wang's contribution to music and recognized Mr. Wang's "History of Chinese Music" and his efforts to popularize music as having the most indelible value. Guo Butao's speech mainly reported on the situation of running a newspaper with Mr. Wang in Sichuan in his early years and praised Mr. Wang's knowledge and personality. Huang Boqiao's speech mainly stated that he had three feelings about attending Mr. Wang's memorial service today: First, why did Mr. Wang give up studying politics and economics and specialize in music? According to our speculation, it may be because he saw that although our country is known as a land of ritual and music, ritual is now lost and music is gone. Second, Mr. Wang has studied in Germany for sixteen years and has never received a penny of subsidy from the government or private sources. This spirit of hard study should be the first among Chinese students studying abroad, making those students who receive public funds or family support but do not work hard feel ashamed. Third, the richness of creation and translation is a pioneer in bridging Eastern and Western cultures. In addition, he also elaborated on the fact that Chinese people do not pay attention to sports and their lives are not rationalized. The meeting adjourned at 11:45 a.m. After the meeting, the guests gathered in the conference room of the National Conservatory of Music to hold a discussion meeting on matters related to commemorating Mr. Wang. Shu Xincheng chaired the meeting and reported on three proposed methods: raising funds for the Wang Guangqi Scholarship to reward rising talents in the music field, publishing a commemorative album, and finding ways to transport and organize the manuscripts and belongings left in Germany. It was decided to expand the organization of the Wang Guangqi Memorial Committee and elect Shu Xincheng, Huang Boqiao, Guo Butao, Xiao Youmei, and Shen Junyi as standing committee members. It was also decided to set the amount of the scholarship at 5,000 yuan as the goal, and the Memorial Committee would plan to raise funds. Donations from friends of Mr. Wang's life and those who sympathize with Mr. Wang's character are welcome. The Shanghai Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, and Shishi Xinbao newspapers were entrusted to collect donations. On the same day, Mr. Wang's manuscripts were displayed at the meeting place for condolence. Excerpts from the elegies sent by various circles are as follows: 1. Elegy from Zhonghua Book Company: "Lifelong hardship, studying in a different land, the most difficult is sixteen years in Germany, without public or private subsidies, everything depends on my own hands, the sea is vast, where to call the soul, only leaving millions of words of manuscripts, dare to be a family and society to mourn, not related to prestige to cry for this person, 3. Elegy from the colleagues of the National Conservatory of Music: "A master admired for generations, with numerous writings, leaving the history of music to benefit the world, spending years studying rhythm, living in a foreign land, Beethoven accompanies you forever in the night," 3. Elegy from Pan Gongzhan: "The overseas wind returns, should not forget the young China, the beacon is urgent by the river, can you leave the musical fire to pass on," 4. Guo Butao's elegy poem: "Since the day I broke the willow on the long embankment, I have remembered your brilliant essays every year, how could I expect the overseas geese to be cut off, and say that the poet turned into a fairy, the events of twenty years ago are bitter, your elegant demeanor is also my teacher, the Zeng Song drifted away and you also passed away, how can I bear to reread the Qingming words," Shen Bao's couplet, "The sound of sheng and crane breaks far away in the sky, Shanghai has a connection that can be mourned, the ivory tablet reaches the foreign land, the heart history is enough for thousands of years," Zai Boqi's couplet, "Specializing in translation, using your talents to confront your lofty ambitions, suffering from a serious illness in a foreign land, incurable and painful spirit,"

The Chinese Child Welfare Association Sends a Letter Reporting the Disaster Situation in Hua County, Henan, with 300,000 Victims Lacking Food and Shelter, Children Sold for Several Yuan Each, a Tragic Situation 102

The Chinese Child Welfare Association previously sent staff member Huang Zhenying to Yanshi, Henan to handle disaster relief for children, which has been quite effective. Now, it has learned that Mr. Huang recently sent a letter to Shanghai describing the disaster situation in Hua County, Henan, stating that there are 300,000 victims in the area, lacking food and shelter. Children are being sold for several yuan each, a tragic situation. Attached is an explanation from Xie Suian, the magistrate of Hua County: "An investigation reveals that Hua County has suffered from flooding for three years. In 1933 and 1934, the government and local charities were able to raise funds for disaster relief. In 1935, heavy rains caused successive disasters, affecting an area of over 50 million acres and 300,000 victims. Food and shelter are lacking, resources are exhausted, and raising funds is difficult. Relief efforts are minimal. The old and weak have already died of starvation, while the strong are taking risks. Former wealthy people are now impoverished. Deaths from starvation, cold, and bandits are heard of every day. The tragic situation is no different from hell on earth. Since the beginning of spring, nine out of ten houses are empty. Land is being sold at a tenth of its value, but there are no buyers. Children are being sold to other regions for only a few yuan. The heartbreaking sight brings tears to one's eyes. In addition, the higher sandy lands have become barren, while the lower lands remain flooded. The wheat harvest is hopeless. The long spring and summer will lead to the demise of the victims who lack clothing and food. I hope that you, the government and charities, will show great compassion and provide prompt relief so that the survivors of the years of disasters can leave behind their offspring and maintain local security. This would be like rebirth for parents and a living Buddha for all. I respectfully lead the victims to offer incense and pray, in the most urgent expectation."

Yu Shun Steamer Returns to Shanghai After a Perilous Journey; Enters Dock Today for Major Repairs; Due to Ice Accumulation at Monkey Reef, Shanghai-Tianjin Route Still Requires Detour 110

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yu Shun steamer departed from Shanghai at 2 PM on January 12th and arrived in Yantai on the 16th. The weather was already very cold, but there was no ice on the sea surface in Yantai. It was not until the 17th, when the ship reached the Zhili Bay, that thick ice was seen. This was the first time the Shanghai steamer encountered ice. The Yu Shun pushed forward through the ice, which was one to two feet thick along the way, for six hours, covering thirty li. At 6:45 PM, the ship became frozen and immobile. After eight hours, the northwest wind blew it towards the Shandong coast, one hundred li from Dagu. The vast ice field was extremely dangerous.

Survival Amidst Death

At this time, the entire crew and passengers, a total of 167 people, were all in fear for their lives. The shipowner, Li Yunqu, took command on the bridge, foregoing food and rest for twenty-five hours. The ship's food supply was running low, and there was only one day's worth of coal left. Shipowner Li, along with Chief Mate Sheng Zengshou and others, resolved to survive amidst death. They first used the bow to ram through the ice. Then, due to the damage to the forward hold by the ice, they switched to using the reverse gear method, using the stern as the bow, and alternately advancing and retreating for fourteen hours of perilous navigation. They managed to reach Dagu at 10 PM at night.

Blocked Upon Arrival at Dagu

On the 18th, upon seeing the Dagu lighthouse, the people felt relieved, knowing that they were only ten nautical miles away from the light. The Yu Shun continued to use stern navigation, pushing through the ice for three hours. Due to the lack of tide and the thickness of the ice, and the absence of a pilot, the ship anchored near the lighthouse. On the morning of the 19th at 10 AM, a pilot arrived and guided the ship to Tanggu to load coal, replenish water, disembark passengers, and replenish food supplies. They departed Tianjin on the 21st to unload cargo and repair the ship. After eight days in Tianjin, they returned to Tanggu on the 29th. At that time, Zhili Bay was completely frozen, with the inland ice being six to seven feet thick, and the offshore ice being three to five feet thick. Tianjin and Tanggu were completely sealed off, and the Yu Shun was blocked from leaving the port for a long time.

Breaking Through the Ice to Return to Shanghai

The Yu Shun was blocked by ice in Tanggu for two months and two days. It was not until the 10th of this month that a pilot suddenly arrived, saying that the ice outside the Dagu port was loose and passable, and the ship could set sail. They departed at 2 AM on the 10th and reached Bohai Bay at 12 PM, but encountered ice again. After three hours, they still could not break through. Because before the 10th, the outer layer of ice outside Dagu had been blown by the northwest wind to Monkey Reef (Hokiat Hs.). The Yu Shun still had difficulty moving forward. The shipowner again used forward and reverse gears, and after half an hour, they managed to break through the ice layer.

Navigating a Detour

Shipowner Li observed the situation. Monkey Reef was piled high with ice like a mountain, and Laotieshan (Rean Ti Shan Pron at Hs.) had also become an ice-covered sea. The Yantai route was cut off. Therefore, he changed the route and headed to Dalian, making a large detour, before heading to Yantai, in order to safely return to Shanghai. However, there were still ice floes between Yantai and Weihaiwei, up to one or two feet thick, floating on the sea. Therefore, the Yu Shun's voyage was still arduous. Upon arriving in Shanghai today and entering the Songkou port, the crew members were overjoyed to see their hometown again.

Entering the Dock Today

Upon arriving in Shanghai, shipowner Li Zhenqu submitted a detailed report on the encounter with the ice to the General Bureau yesterday afternoon. Mr. Li told reporters that the Shanghai-Tianjin route is currently still difficult to navigate directly. Ships going to Tianjin must not travel via Monkey Reef and must take a detour. The Bureau decided to temporarily suspend the Yu Shun's operations due to concerns about ice damage to the hull, and it will enter the dock for inspection and repairs today. Insurance companies will also be notified to send ship surveyors to inspect the ship. Mr. Li said that the coldest temperature in Dagu was twenty-four degrees below the freezing point. The Yu Shun burned two furnaces continuously, but the water bucket next to the furnace was still frozen solid, which shows the severity of the cold.

Fu Tai Timber Firm and Others Accuse Li Shaobin; Investigating Official Adjourns Hearing for Further Inquiry 111

The Fu Tai and other timber firms on Guangfu Road in Zhabei have recently been involved in a dispute over house tax materials. The timber industry association once staged a strike, which was mediated by the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The previous report detailed these events. It is now known that Chen Hongzhang, manager of Fu Tai Timber Firm, and Huang Xingsheng, manager of Yuan Xing Timber Firm, have engaged lawyer Xu Zuoliang to file a private prosecution with the Criminal Court of the District Court, accusing Li Shaobin, director of the North Shanghai Inspection Office of the Finance Bureau, of abusing his authority and obstructing freedom. The accusation states that Li Shaobin knowingly imposed forced collection of donations when they should not have been collected. The accusation states that Chen Hongzhang, manager of Fu Tai Timber Firm, was assessed by Li Shaobin, director of the North Shanghai Inspection Office, for house tax of 50 yuan per quarter in the 23rd year and 85 yuan per quarter in the 24th year, and was ordered to pay a supplementary donation of 407 yuan and 68 cents, as well as a fine of 81 yuan and 54 cents. Chen Hongzhang felt that the tax on horses and houses was too high and unaffordable. Upon inquiring, he learned that more than ten companies in the same industry were suffering from the heavy tax burden. He requested the Shanghai Timber Industry Association to negotiate with the Municipal Finance Bureau. While the petition was in progress, Chen Qizhang was suddenly summoned by the police on the 3rd of this month at 12:00 PM to the office and detained for failing to pay. He was released on bail on the afternoon of the 4th after the Timber Industry Association intervened. Huang Xingsheng, the agent of Yuan Xing Timber Firm, was assessed based on the unilaterally determined recent rental price of the North Shanghai Inspection Office, calculating the house tax at 14 percent, resulting in a tax of 462 yuan, plus a 20 percent fine of 92 yuan and 40 cents. The defendant is now forcibly collecting donations and fines totaling a huge sum of 902 yuan, 1 dime and 6 cents, as evidenced by receipts, and forced the plaintiffs to sign a voluntary document promising to pay the donations. The recent rental price of the Fu Tai Timber Firm, which Chen Qizhang represents, is calculated at 198 yuan per month, resulting in an annual donation of 330 yuan, 9 dimes and 1 cent. The defendant is now forcibly collecting donations and fines totaling 489 yuan, 2 dimes and 2 cents. The defendant intentionally imposed forced collection in violation of Article 5 of the Regulations for Investigating House Rentals, and the defendant should be found guilty of violating Articles 129 and 302 of the Criminal Law. After receiving the accusation, the court held a hearing yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM in the Criminal Court No. 12, presided over by Judge Lu Hongyi. Chen Qizhang testified that he was 27 years old, from Ningbo. On the 3rd of this month, at 12:00 PM, the police took him to the collection office, and at 6:00 PM, he was transferred to the Second Precinct of the Fourth District Police Station for overnight detention. The next day, he was transferred to the North Station Branch Bureau, and at 1:00 PM, he was released on bail after being sent to the General Bureau. The defendant abused his authority and detained his body for 28 hours, depriving him of his freedom of movement. He requested that the law be thoroughly investigated. Li Shaobin testified that he was 47 years old, from Yunnan, and served as the director of the Zhabei Collection Office. The Guangfu Road Fu Tai Timber Firm concealed the value of the leased land, falsely claiming to own the property, and reported 50 yuan per quarter for land and house tax. After the Municipal Finance Bureau sent personnel to investigate, it was found that the timber firm's land, storage, etc., were actually leased from others, with an annual rental price of 2,000 yuan, and four houses were built on the land, valued at 8 yuan each. Therefore, the timber firm should pay a total of 407 yuan, 6 dimes and 8 cents for land and house tax, plus a fine of 81 yuan, 5 dimes and 4 cents. Collection had been unsuccessful despite repeated attempts, so he handled it in accordance with the regulations, and there was nothing improper. He was asked whether he had gone to assess the value. He replied that the Finance Bureau had sent personnel to conduct an on-site inspection. He was asked whether the pursuit of fines was his idea. He replied that it was not, and that he was executing orders. The questioning was adjourned for further inquiry as it was late.

Japanese Man Shops Without Paying, Tries to Harm Chinese Police Officer 112

According to the Japanese newspaper "Mainichi Shimbun," Nishiyama Toshihiko, from Nishi Awara Village, Ibo County, Hyogo Prefecture, Japan, is currently a clerk at Takeuchi Print Shop at No. 304 Haining Road in Shanghai. At 4:40 AM on the 15th, he bought a package of chocolate candy worth 2 dimes from the North Wanfeng Chinese cigarette and paper shop at No. 499 North Sichuan Road. After the shop assistant, Zhang Wenzhong, handed him the candy, he asked him to pay. Unexpectedly, Nishiyama claimed that he had already paid and tried to leave with the candy. Zhang accused him of cheating and asked him to return the candy. Nishiyama became violent and slapped Zhang's cheek. The two began to argue loudly. A police officer from the Public Security Bureau, who was stationed nearby, saw the commotion and tried to mediate. To everyone's surprise, Nishiyama also tried to attack the police officer. The police officer had no choice but to take him to the Public Security Bureau and hand him over to the Japanese Consulate Police Station. It was discovered that Nishiyama had previously stabbed a Chinese person with a kitchen knife at a Chinese restaurant on Avenue Joffre, and had repeatedly committed illegal acts. Therefore, the Japanese Police Station will impose a severe punishment on him.

Abduction of a Woman Foiled Mid-Route; Seen by Abducted Child's Uncle 113

Lin Di, the eleven-year-old niece of Ye Zhengqi, a native of Anqing living at No. 9, Alley 80, Route Frelupt, was playing at the entrance of the alley at around 2 PM the day before yesterday. A woman named Li Wangshi (47 years old, native of Anhui, living at No. 59 on the same road) tricked her into going to the theater by hiring a rickshaw. Unexpectedly, while traveling to the entrance of Hengqing Alley on Route Paul Beau, Ye Zhengqi and his friend Xu Wenbin happened to pass by and saw her. Wondering why his niece was riding in a rickshaw with an unfamiliar woman, he immediately stopped them to inquire. Unexpectedly, the woman dared to impersonate the girl's mother, claiming, "I'm taking my own daughter out for a stroll. What does it have to do with you?" At this point, the abduction was discovered. They grabbed and restrained the woman. Shen Xianxi, a constable, arrived and took Li Wangshi and the girl to the police station. After questioning by the detective, Wangshi confessed to the attempted abduction. Lin Di said that the woman had given her a bag of fruit one day and asked her to wait for her at the entrance of the alley again today, preparing to go to the theater together. She didn't know it was an abduction. Yesterday afternoon, Wangshi was sent to the First Special District Court, Criminal Division One. The police station's lawyer requested a postponement to investigate whether the defendant had committed any other crimes. Judge Wang approved the postponement and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody.

Granddaughter Disputes Inheritance 114

The late Inspector Ji Sheng of the French Police Station, who lived at No. 14 Pingjihe Road in the French Concession, owned a self-built house. In his later years, he adopted Gu Weiyi as his only son due to a lack of descendants. Therefore, all of Ji Sheng's inheritance was received by Gu Weiyi. Recently, Gao Rong Qiaolin, the 35-year-old granddaughter of Ji Sheng (native of Cixi, Zhejiang), engaged lawyer Xu Zuyan to file a lawsuit with the Second Special District Court, Civil Division, to confirm that the plaintiff Rong Qiaolin has the right to inherit. The application for litigation assistance has been approved by the court. Yesterday, the court summoned the parties. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the plaintiff is the granddaughter of Gu Jisheng's eldest daughter, married to Gao Yongquan. Gu Jisheng passed away on the 13th day of the eighth month of the old calendar last year. According to the Civil Code, inheritance naturally begins. It has been found that the total value of the grandfather's inheritance is three to four hundred thousand yuan. The plaintiff's mother is the biological daughter of the grandfather Gu Jisheng. The defendant, Gu Weiyi, is the adopted son of the grandfather Gu Jisheng. According to law, the adopted son should receive one-third of the property, and the plaintiff should receive two-thirds. Secondly, the plaintiff and her husband are poor and unable to pay the litigation costs, so they should be granted litigation assistance. The defendant Gu Weiyi's lawyer, Wang Henggu, stated that the plaintiff had filed a lawsuit in this case in February last year. At that time, Chen Sanlin, Wang Wenkui, and the lawyers for both parties, Hu Jue and Suan Yaoxian, mediated a settlement, whereby the defendant Gu Weiyi paid Rong Qiaolin 23,000 yuan to resolve the matter. A settlement agreement was signed, completely waiving all rights of the parties and stating that no further disputes would arise. The agreement was signed on February 21st, and the case was dismissed on the 22nd. How can the plaintiff now file a lawsuit again? Furthermore, the defendant paid the plaintiff 23,000 yuan at that time, which was a substantial amount. Why is it necessary to apply to this court for litigation assistance? The plaintiff's claim should be dismissed. The plaintiff's lawyer further stated that although the plaintiff received a large sum of money at that time, she had many debts and had to repay them, so she now has nothing left. The settlement agreement signed by both parties did not state that she waived her right to inheritance. Judge Ma Yishu concluded the debate and ruled in court that the plaintiff's litigation assistance was approved.

(B) The executive committee decided to return the advance payments and requested ratification. Approved. (C) The new standardized measuring instruments should be uniformly adopted. It was resolved to investigate those who have not used them, provide scales from the association, and order them to be replaced. After discussing multiple temporary proposals, the meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Ji Ren Assistance Association Handles Coffin Materials; 25 Yuan Coffin and Funeral Expenses per Corpse 119

The Ji Ren Assistance Association in Shanghai provides coffins worth 20 yuan, as well as lime, charcoal ash, and carrying fees to poor and underprivileged compatriots who cannot afford coffins and burials. It avoids the form of charity in its implementation and has a history of eighteen years. Since Mr. Shao Ruxin resumed his duties, he has actively reorganized and expanded the association. The first members' dinner was held at Gongdelin on the evening of the 15th, and the association's affairs were reported. More than 100 male and female members attended, including Li Linshu, Lu Guanhong, Wu Renbao, Liu Yan, Yang Senshan, Fei Shaojin, and Ms. Zhou Ruiying. Chairman Shao Ruxin began by reporting that it is quite difficult to run a charity in the midst of the current economic downturn. It is proposed to change the funding of the recognized expenses as follows: Regular expenses will be borne by the board of directors separately. The cost of materials will be borne by the members, with one thousand people forming a team to assist in providing materials for one coffin. The cost of materials, including charcoal ash, lime, and carrying fees, totals 25 yuan. Therefore, each member only needs to contribute 2.5 cents, and one thousand people contribute 25 yuan. If one coffin is replaced, there will never be a shortage in the basic 400 coffins. Member recognition is easy and effortless. Special expenses are reserved for expanding the material production field and the public cemetery, and will be collected separately. No donations will be solicited from outside. The new regulations will be printed and sent to all members to solicit opinions and convene a meeting at a fixed time for public decision-making and implementation. A dinner was then held, and the event ended at 9:00 PM.

A New Ghost Under a Bus Wheel: Sun Aqing Under Investigation by the Police 125

Wang Wenan, a 24-year-old Wuxi native residing at 655 Huishan Road, and currently working as an artist at the Universal Film Company on Fuzhou Road, was riding his bicycle with friends Wang Acai, Hua Shouxing, and others around 7 AM the day before, planning to go to New Shanghai for recreation. As they traveled west to east near the intersection of Huade Road and Meizhou Road, a No. 15050 Route Ten public bus driven by Sun Aqing came speeding from behind. Unable to brake in time, the front left wheel collided with the rear wheel of Wang Wenan's bicycle, causing him to fall to the ground, suffering severe head injuries and dying shortly thereafter. Police arrived after being notified and instructed detectives Zhang Tieshan and others from the Yangshupu Police Station to inspect the scene. The body was then taken to the autopsy room on Feitoul Road. The First Special District Court dispatched Prosecutor Zhang Zongru, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zujing, to examine the body the day before. Detective Zhang first reported the circumstances, and Sun Aqing stated that he had been a public bus driver for three years. He claimed that his bus was initially ahead of the deceased, but the deceased suddenly overtook him. At that moment, another vehicle was approaching from the opposite direction, and the deceased swerved left in front of his bus to avoid it, making it impossible for him to brake, resulting in the collision. Wang Acai testified that he was riding in the lead, Hua Shouxing was second, and the deceased was behind Hua. All three of them were in front of the bus when it sped up from behind without honking the horn and hit the deceased. He also said there were no cars coming from the opposite direction. Hua Shouxing testified that he heard the crash and looked back, seeing that the bus did not immediately stop. His testimony was similar to Wang Acai's. After taking the statements, Zhang concluded that Wang Wenan, male, died from a head injury sustained after being struck by the No. 15050 Route Ten public bus. The body was released to his brother Wang Wei for burial after signing an undertaking. The police will investigate whether bus driver Sun Aqing was negligent.

Kidnapping of a Boy for Ransom 130

Ni Heshang from Tongzhou, residing at No. 32 Gui'an Lane, Senyin Road in the South City, sneaked into Dean Lane, Pengpu Road in Yangshupu around 3 PM on November 10th last year and lured Wang Liu's five-year-old son, Gengsheng, from the same hometown, to his father Ni Siyuan's home in Zhangxing Town, Laohong Port in his hometown. He then falsely claimed to Wang Liu that her son had been kidnapped by Ni Futang and that she would have to pay 40 yuan to get him back. Wang Liu realized he was behind it and pretended to agree to raise the money, secretly following him to Gui'an Lane. She learned the truth from Ni Futang and reported to the Yulin Road Police Station. Detective Li Hongsheng was secretly dispatched, together with the police officers from the Public Security Bureau in charge, and arrested him at the address and brought him back to the police station. He was sent to the First Special District Court. He was evasive in his confession and was detained. The day before, Judge Jiang Shuzi continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. The Public Security Bureau lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that Wang Liu had appeared in court to testify and proved that she had gone to the defendant's home in Zhangxing Town, Laohong Port, Tongzhou, and saw her son, Gengsheng, crying and calling for his mother. She intended to take him back to Shanghai, but his father accused her of being a kidnapper and went with her to the local police station. She explained the situation, but she was unable to bring Gengsheng back and had to return to Shanghai. She and the defendant used to live in the same neighborhood near Laoximen, he was a coppersmith, and they were neighbors with no improper relationship. After her husband passed away last spring, he left her son, Gengsheng, and others. When questioned, the defendant insisted that he had known her for years and admitted to taking the child to his hometown to be raised by his father Ni Siyuan. He admitted that he wanted to extort 40 yuan from her to bring the child back. Judge Jiang ordered a postponement and will send a letter to the Nantong Local Court to bring Wang's child Gengsheng to Shanghai for collection and further verification.

Lawsuit Over Detained 10,000 Yuan Deposit: Scheduled for Sentencing 133

Han Yulin, manager of the Pingyuan Coal Sales Agency, and Li Shencang, residing at No. 8 Fen'an Lane, West Huade Road, entered into a coal transportation contract on August 4th of the year before last. The contract stipulated that Li would transport the coal from the agency and would provide a deposit of 10,000 yuan. Di Yiping, under the name of Houming, deposited the money in the savings department of the China Industrial Bank, with both Li and Han's seals affixed to the deposit. In the future, the money could only be withdrawn with the joint seals of Li, Han, and Di. Li kept the savings passbook. After signing the contract, a year passed, and Pinghou did not deliver any coal to Li for transportation. After Li negotiated with Han, they decided to cancel the contract. Li then took the passbook to the China Industrial Bank to withdraw the deposit, but the bank, at the request of Western doctor Niu Huilin, refused to pay. It turned out that Pinghou Coal Sales Agency had asked Dr. Niu to act as a guarantor and had a credit line with the business department of the China Industrial Bank. They owed the bank 10,300 yuan and had been repeatedly urged to pay. Pinghou could not repay the debt, so they turned to Dr. Niu to fulfill his guarantor duties. Dr. Niu, fearing financial loss, learned from an employee of Pinghou surnamed Wu that there was another 10,000 yuan deposit in the bank. He immediately sent a letter requesting that the deposit be used to offset the debt, causing Li Shencang to not receive a single penny. Therefore, Li filed a lawsuit against Shen Guangyan, the person in charge of savings at the bank, requesting an order to return the deposit and pay the interest. Han Yulin, the manager of Pinghou, sympathized with Li and joined the lawsuit. Niu Huilin sympathized with the China Industrial Bank and also joined the lawsuit. It seemed that both parties had assistants. The First Special District Court concluded the first trial and ruled against Li Shencang, determining that the ownership of the deposit had belonged to Pinghou and allowing the defendant to deduct it from Pinghou's debt. Li, dissatisfied with the judgment, hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, stating reasons and requesting the original judgment be overturned. Both sides' participants still maintained their old interests and positions. Yesterday afternoon, the Second Branch of the High Court convened a collegial panel for trial. First, Jiang Yiping, the attorney for appellant Li Zhongcang, argued that the issue in the case was the ownership of the 10,000 yuan deposit. The appellant believed that the ownership of the money had not been transferred to Pinghou. Although the deposit slip was in Pinghou's name, it still bore the seals of both Li Shencang and Han Yulin. Since the coal transportation contract was signed through legal procedures and Pinghou could not fulfill the contract, the deposit should be returned. How could it be used to offset Pinghou's debt? The China Industrial Bank initially had no intention of offsetting the debt. It only did so after being entrusted by Niu. Bank practices place the most importance on seals on deposit slips. Li and Pinghou had no relationship. That the money was deposited in Pinghou's name with his seal and Han's joint seal should have been known to the bank from the start. This proves that it was a conditional deposit. Niu was a guarantor for other debts of Pinghou. The bank could demand repayment from Pinghou and Niu separately. It should not confuse right and wrong. Therefore, he dared not say that the intentions of the bank and Dr. Niu were pure. Thus, he appealed. Subsequently, the attorney for the appellee, Wang Fuchang, and the attorney for Niu Huilin rebutted, stating that the deposit slip clearly stated that the depositor was Pinghou, so the money belonged to Pinghou. Although Li and Han's seals were affixed, they were affixed under Pinghou's name. The format of the seal was like the seal of the court on a document below the court's official seal. It cannot be considered that the seal implies that the person who put the seal on is the depositor. Judge Han then declared the debate concluded and scheduled the sentencing for the afternoon of the 21st of this month.

The Fine Editions of Works by Unmatched Philosophers of Wuxi Will be Finely Printed 136

The Zhenjiang Provincial Library recently held a cultural relics exhibition. More than 17,000 people visited the exhibition, making it an unprecedented event in the provincial capital. These include the Yuan-era engraved edition of Ni Yunlin's poetry collection, the Ming-era engraved edition of Gao Zi's Posthumous Writings, the Kangxi-era engraved editions of Gao Zi's Posthumous Goodness and Gao Zi's Literary Collection, Gao Zi's Poetry Collection, Confucius' Interpretation of Spring and Autumn, Confucius' Interpretation of Book of Changes, the Ming-era Shao Wenzhuang's Summary of Public Documents, History of Learning, Zuo Zhuan, the Ming-era Qin Songling's Collection of Cangxian Hermit, Qian Surun's Essentials of the Book of Documents, Zhang Yunluan's Four Books, Classic Revisions, Gu Xiancheng's Jinggao Collection, Zhang Xuan's Remaining Loyal Admonitions, Gu Guangxu's Xiangquan Collection, Zou Fang'e's First Draft of the Daya Hall, Bao Ting's Manuscript of the Reading Study, Hua Xuequan's Questioning Doubts in Spring and Autumn, Shi Xuejian's Manuscript from One Branch Studio, Hua Wengui's Poems from Leisurely Chanting, Yang Piao's Collection of Shuangwutong Pavilion, Zou Yigui's Small Mountain Poetry, Yang Fangcan's First Draft of the Zhenshuaizhai, Zhu Yunjun's Painting Villa Manuscripts, Liu Jian's Self-cultivation Studio Notes, Yan Shengsun's Autumn Water Collection and others. All were originally engraved at that time and are rare in modern times. Even the libraries in Wuxi rarely have them. It is said that some people plan to gather a large amount of money to have them printed in lithography to spread them widely.

Report of the Guangdong-Guangxi Industrial Survey Group (4) 146

— Yang'an

Sent from Guangzhou

China's Greatest Southern University

On the second day of arriving in Guangdong, I was invited by President Zou Haibin to visit the National Sun Yat-sen University, which he runs. Mr. Zou first briefly described the history of the school to his colleagues. The school was founded in the spring of the thirteenth year of the Republic of China. Mr. Sun Yat-sen ordered Mr. Zou to merge and reorganize the National Guangdong Higher Teachers College, the Guangdong Public Law College, and the Public Agricultural College, establishing four departments of liberal arts, sciences, law, and agriculture. Later, he took over the Public Medical College and added a medical department. Mr. Sun Yat-sen believed that the original school buildings were scattered in the urban area, which was not suitable for factory repairs and difficult to develop. He asked Mr. Zou to choose Shipai as the new school site. Construction began in March of the 22nd year, and both phases of the project were completed in thirty months. The five colleges of agriculture, engineering, law, liberal arts, and sciences have all moved in one after another. There are currently more than 2,000 students, with females accounting for one-tenth. The situation is that Baiyun Mountain surrounds it and the Pearl River surrounds it. The area inside the school has undulating hills and rippling ponds. The areas are divided and named after the provinces of our country. In addition, the hills and pools in each area are named after the mountains, rivers, and lakes in the provinces. The entire school covers an area of 30,000 acres. Except for the buildings, all are farmland. Each college and dormitory has room for expansion. The fruit tree plan is long-term. There are currently 4.5 million trees planted. After three or four years, 500,000 trees will mature first. If each tree is valued at one yuan per year, then 500,000 yuan can be obtained annually. After ten years, all 4.5 million trees will be profitable, and 4.5 million yuan can be obtained. Mr. Zou said that the school wants to make the education that has always been consumptive into productive education. His intentions are profound. Foreigners who come here all consider it to be China's cultural city. A certain Japanese ambassador visited the school and was able to complete such a large-scale school building in a short period of time with 500,000 yuan. The Japanese were amazed by the cost savings, the speed of the project, and the greatness of the scale. The achievements of each college have their own characteristics, such as the agricultural college's rice crop improvement and silkworm experiments. The law college has an economic survey office to investigate farmers' lives and price indexes, and a public legal advisory office to provide free legal advice to the people. The engineering college pays attention to practical training, with fifteen or sixteen hours of practical training each week. President Zou said that the school is thinking about self-reliance and economic independence in the future. In eight or ten years, it can survive even if the doors are closed. The current plan to plant fruit trees has been realized, and vegetables, pig farming, chicken farming, and cattle farming are being implemented. In the future, everything can be achieved without problems, except for coal and salt, which cannot be self-sufficient. For national crisis education, military training and air defense exercises are given the same attention, and many of the courses have been changed. I highly praised the greatness of the school's architecture. Mr. Zou said that he really has three fears here. The magnificent school building is used to enrich its brilliance, promote learning, and contribute to the country and society. If there is only material and no spirit, it is a waste of national funds and a waste of people's resources. That is one fear. The suitability of the school building is for students to easily hide and cultivate themselves. If they are content with comfort, they will not be able to endure hardship in the future. Even those who come from the fields will not be able to return to the fields, then the establishment of this school is no different from training disabled people. That is the second fear. A large amount of planting is for productive education, or they may not cherish it and destroy it, or the management may not be good and the income may not be as expected. Not only will the productive education not be completed in the future, but people will regard production as a daunting task. That is the third fear. Mr. Zou's words are very respectable. I said that this school will make education and industry into one piece. The technical talents recently created are all used locally, which is valuable. Our visit to the highest university in the south took four hours. The north and south are hundreds of miles apart. If it were not for using a car, I am afraid that it would not be possible to complete the visit in two or three days. Dr. Zheng Yanfen, Dean of the Law School, served in the League of Nations for many years. When he returned to China the year before last, Ambassador Gu Shaochuan prepared a letter of introduction to me. I was not able to meet him when I went to Jiangxi. I did not expect to meet him here today. He told me in great detail about the content of the school. I will write another article about it when I have time.

Spring and Autumn

Little Fun 147

— (Qian Shan)

"Talk big, spend little money" is a proverb from the old capital. For example, one "diao" (a string of cash) means ten copper coins, or five twenty-copper coins. Five hundred "qian" or "wen" means only five ten-copper coins. However, in Shandong and other provinces, it is the opposite. One "diao" means one hundred ten-copper coins. This may be based on the old-fashioned coins. I recall that when I was in Beijing more than ten years ago, there were many small copper coins made to represent paper money, with red copper representing five "wen," red copper representing two "wen," and yellow copper representing one "wen," and the texture was very fine. At that time, one or two "wen" of small copper coins could really buy some scallions, ginger, pepper, and garlic as ingredients, and five "wen" could prepare oil, salt, sauce, and vinegar for seasoning! Such a small expense felt interesting even just mentioning it, let alone when beggars came to the door asking for alms, just one small copper coin would send them away. Even if you sent away ten beggars a day, it would cost one copper coin! Thinking about it now, it is very funny!

The Gray City 148

— Xie Zhongwen

If London is the city of fog, then Beijing should be considered the city of gray. Just like the density and dirtiness of the gray, my impression of Beijing is deep and clear. But the most unforgettable thing for me is gray.

In Beijing, whether going out or staying at home, gray entangled me everywhere. On the road it flew into my ears and nose, and as soon as I entered the hutong, it would bury my instep. Even in the house, it would slip in through the cracks in the windows and scatter on the tables, chairs, beds, and books. Even the White Pagoda towering in Beihai Park, the magnificent Forbidden City, and the crystal clear Kunming Lake all had to be sprinkled with a layer of subtle decolorizer. Gray floated to every place I went, and gray also squeezed into every corner of Beijing.

This ancient northern country is so full of gray, gray, gray. Maybe it is gray, this dirty thing, that makes the northern country age? But it once seduced the eyes of tourists!

Gray not only enveloped the entire outline of Beijing, but also penetrated its core, making everything alive in its embrace dizzy, numb, and lazy!

I saw skinny donkeys and camels carrying charcoal, half-opening their eyes and walking slowly. I saw big carts loaded with tall straw, with carters lying on the straw napping. I saw idlers carrying birdcages and strolling around the Temple of the Emperors morning and evening. I saw apartments, restaurants, ballrooms, and movie theaters packed with students rushing to join the fun. I saw many wandering souls who had lost their vitality. I saw the gray on the soul of Beijing!

This indelible gray on the soul is increasing its accumulation, and one day it will submerge this ancient northern country, right? Cursable gray!

The Cellar of Beijing 149

— Chou Cheng

Yesterday I received a letter from my old friend Mr. Huang, who came from Hebei, detailing the cellars of Beijing. I transcribe it as follows to share with readers:

The northern land is severely cold. Once winter arrives, the climate is harsh, the ground has no green grass, and among the crops that can overwinter in the ground, only wheat seedlings exist, but their leaves are also frozen and brittle. As for vegetables and fruits, in this period, it can be said that all traces have disappeared from the fields. It was my first time traveling to the north for the winter, and seeing this situation, I was initially worried about the disruption of the winter vegetable supply. However, since winter began, the cook has continued to serve them daily, and I have long forgotten about it. At the end of the twelfth month, I wanted to see what the northern customs were like for the Lunar New Year, so I bravely ventured into the city despite the cold (because I am afraid of the cold, I have been indoors by the stove all day since winter began and have never entered the city). I saw fresh vegetables filling the market. Vendors were carrying them in carts and on their shoulders, hawking along the streets. Not only were all kinds of vegetables that had disappeared from the fields readily available, but even fresh fruits such as watermelons, cucumbers, grapes, persimmons, and pears, which ripen in summer and autumn, were available for purchase. I tried buying them and eating them, and I felt that their color, aroma, and crispness were no different from those picked from the branches and harvested from the fields. They were not like Liu Ji's oranges, dry as worn-out wadding, so I couldn't help but be suspicious. Then I questioned the locals and learned that the common people had a special method of long-term storage. The method is very simple: the farmers here choose a gap in their courtyards, dig a well with a diameter of about three feet, and a depth of more than ten feet, and then dig horizontally to create an earth room. The width of the room varies depending on the amount of stored goods. The larger ones need to be supported by thick boards and wooden pillars to prevent collapse. There is a ladder inside for people to ascend and descend, and a rope is used to lower things in and out. The wellhead is often covered with wooden boards to prevent air circulation, and then covered with dry grass, two or three feet thick, which is called a "cellar," pronounced like "jiao" in the northern language. Usually, when farmers have a harvest, they put anything they want to keep fresh in it after picking it. Once winter arrives, they take all that is in the fields and store it in the cellar. After that, they take it out to eat as needed, and it does not change its freshness for a long time. If properly stored, the life of vegetables and fruits can be extended for a year in the cellar, awaiting the transfer of new and old crops. And the original color, aroma, sweetness, and crispness do not change at all. This kind of cellar is extremely common in North China. Except for cities, almost every household in the countryside has one. But it is still questionable whether we can imitate this in the south. Because the soil layer in the south is thin and the water table is close, digging can easily turn into a water well. If there is no such concern, then the reputation of fruits in the south will definitely be far superior to canned fresh vegetables. Because today's so-called canned fruits have been scientifically processed, and cannot be compared with the old-fashioned candied fruits, but in fact, the color, aroma, sweetness, and crispness of canned fruits have all been lost. They must be cooked and put into cans, which is similar to the method of making candied fruits. The only difference is the addition of a can. Therefore, instead of calling them canned fresh fruits, it is more accurate to call them canned candied fruits. If the northern method of cellar storage can be promoted in the south, I know that the value of cellar products will definitely surpass that of canned products.

Little Western Heaven 150

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Four: Heavy Profit, Beautiful Woman, Mercenary Husband Reluctantly Loves; Lofty Ambitions, Strong Feet, Robust Man Flees into Wilderness

Li Shilian reached into his arms, seemingly fumbling for the manuscript in his arms, then raised his hand again and scratched his hair a few times, and then answered with a smile: Rather than waiting here at Mr. Cheng's place, and disturbing Mr. Cheng, I might as well wait for Mr. Wang in my own house, so I can have a pleasant chat. Zhiqian smiled and said: If Bei Hai comes, I will definitely ask him to visit you. But I have a word outside of the topic to tell you. I know Wang Beihai's temper. He is a young man after all. If you want him to help, just ask him to help. As long as it is within reason, I don't think he will refuse. But you must not use something as leverage to move him, as an exchange condition. Li Shilian could not help but blush when he heard these words. He also pulled on his lapels a couple of times, as if Zhiqian's words had touched a sore spot. Li Shilian smiled and said: My report is like this. But if you want to be a matchmaker, that is your good intention. Whether Bei Hai accepts it or not is another matter. But if you don't put these two things together, I think Bei Hai will definitely not blame you. Although a look of hesitation constantly appeared on Li Shilian's face, he quietly listened to Zhiqian's words. After he finished speaking, he stood up and cupped his hands and smiled: I understand, I understand. In the future, when things are successful, everyone will ask Mr. Cheng to have a drink. After finishing, he left happily with a smile. Zhiqian walked around the room for a while, and then wrote a note and put it on the table. It said: Brother Bei Hai is here, quickly go to Mr. Li Shilian's house to negotiate something. He himself half-closed the door and came to sit idly in Zhou Yourong's room in front. There were two other people in suits sitting in his room. Judging by their clothes, although they were dark blue, they had a layer of non-red or yellow color on the outside. It was clear that they were used to running around on the mainland, covered with a layer of dust. Zhou Yourong stood up first and smiled: I was just planning to ask you to come, and you came, that's great. He introduced the two of them, saying that one was Guo Zhuoran, the head of the Western Travel Group, and the other was Cheng Shigong, the deputy head of the group. Mr. Guo had a slightly pointed face, and his cheeks were covered with short beard. Because the beard was also a yellowish-red color, it seemed that it was also covered with dust. However, next to his high nose bridge, his two sparkling eyes could very well represent his adventurous spirit. (416)

Praising Peace 151

— Fire

Lying in bed. No home, no soul; because being caught under the huge gears, would it allow you to think? So, in order to still live; very simply, I only want to open my tired eyelids a little more like a... grub. So, a light dream embraces the aching waist, in the tearful night. Even if strange and bizarre, it is joyful, nostalgic, for the stimulation that is not found in the world.

I will step into the realm I hope for, suddenly!

As if being in the hometown I had been separated from for seven years, now with only a hair's breadth of distance, finally imprinted on the lingering and confused eardrums, this first sound with the smell of sulfur... the sound of gunfire.

Opening my eyes does not seem necessary, anyway, it is a piece of moaning, crying, no! no! like the hoot of an owl heard in the middle of the night.

Paper money, illuminated by the green of the electric flower, is like a will-o'-the-wisp; if there were no choking sounds, I would suspect that I had already been sleeping in a stone tomb.

"Our people from the Northeast should kowtow facing the Northeast."

"Yes! Light a candle."

"I'll stand in the middle!"

So, they set off firecrackers, and then I remembered that it was New Year's Eve. So, I remembered that Chahar East was again a local issue. So, deeply, like reading letters from friends in rural areas, it seems that "not only can't you find cash in the village now, it's even difficult to scrape together fifty yuan in banknotes," a dance of ink.

Then I heard the boss in the apartment calling his little girl to kowtow, and then they set off firecrackers again, and then the sounds of heaven-shaking explosions echoed far and near, and then singing and dancing of peace and prosperity.

Then the courtyard was quiet, and then the goddess of dreams covered my leaping chest with black gauze.

So, praising peace. (Note: "Praising Peace" is a common inscription with gold letters on a black background seen on the stage of temples in my hometown when I was a child.)

Three Talks on Interviews 152

— Kong Jie

In various examinations, in addition to the written test, there is often an interview section. Although it seems unimportant, it should not be ignored. I recently heard three things from a friend that are sufficient to prove this:

A certain company planned to recruit three trainees. For a time, a large number of people signed up, but only eight people passed the written test. Therefore, the company decided to interview these eight people in the morning. All eight people went on time, but the manager did not appear, only giving each person a bowl of wontons. When they were summoned, they were only asked, "How many wontons did you eat?" Only three people could answer, so only these three were hired.

Another factory recruited several supervisors. After the written test was completed, the qualified candidates were summoned one by one and asked to pass through a narrow passage to reach the interview location. On the road, there was a stool and a dustpan. Each candidate stepped over them, but only one person helped them up and placed them in the corner. Because this person could manage trivial matters and was detail-oriented, he was suitable for the position of supervisor and was hired.

A certain lady applied for a typist interview. The lady usually dressed very plainly, but she dressed up specially on this day. However, the examiner was afraid that she would not be content with the small salary, which led to her being rejected. The position was obtained by another candidate who was not as talented as the lady.

The Five Colors of Beiping 153

— Luo Man

Beiping is a political district, a cultural city, a display of ancient relics, and a dyeing vat mixed with sin.

Red is dyed on women's lips, freshly like a funnel dripping with blood, fox-like, held on men's arms, and men leisurely stroll as if carrying a cane. In the setting sun and lamplight of the guard's head, in the crowded city streets, this red color is particularly distinct. As long as cunning eyes weave back and forth, then in a charming smile, this red color seems to be selling the mark of flesh and soul.

Yellow is dyed on the walls of each house in the alleys. When the sun is sleepy and tired, various boys and girls emerge from under each wall, with messy hair and sweaty faces, squatting there and vigorously excreting this yellow dye. Sometimes, a snotty hand holds a branch and plays with its own creations. When tired of playing, they scold each other across the street. Xiao Shunzi scolds Wang Ni's mother for sleeping with Wang Laizi, and Wang Ni scolds Agou's sister for walking on the street with men. Then, in a cacophony, everyone scolds each other's mothers until a faint lamplight dyes the whole street, and everyone's mother comes out and scolds her own child's mother and goes in. Thus, two rows of yellow things are displayed on the street, making a precious decoration for this ancient city. Suddenly, two dogs bark and start fighting again.

Blue is dyed on the police's small stick in the center of the street. With a gentle lift and a whoosh, a car carrying a few pieces of glamorous flesh flies by; this blue stick lifts again, and a few more pieces of glamorous flesh fly by. The car seems to be disappointed without this decoration, and the witch-like woman in the car is always laughing. However, there are also times when the blue stick is raised and no car passes by. However, this stick happens to fall on the head of a rickshaw puller, so the rickshaw puller cannot but admit that this small stick is their authority.

White is painted on the faces of young people. After the fashionable urban girls and young masters get up at eleven o'clock, they must first wash their faces and then thickly apply face cream; what powder, what water, they always choose brands from Paris; in their hearts, they are indeed biting this white thing on their faces and living a romantic life. Although everyone says that applying it too white looks like a fairy, snow cream, still has a strong appeal. Which poor girl doesn't stand in front of the shop window in a daze?

Black is dyed on the faces, hands, nostrils, and hearts of coal miners. They seem to be destined to be black, moving like Indian Ah San, always so dull as if they have no human feelings. In the morning, when it is still very dark, they have to shrink their black heads and black hands to climb up. Black coal is loaded into black carts, and frozen, stiff hands hold the whip and lash the panting livestock, then they hang their heads and doze off, and the cart slowly crawls along the dusty road. They have no youth, no life, and life is just a rigid sacrifice in this black, trembling color.

——This Beiping, such a big dyeing vat, also dyes various colors of sin, symbolizing the essence of various lives. As long as you are a thoughtful person, you can definitely see the true colors and true face of Beiping in these colors.

Educational News

Education Department Promulgates Revised Registration Rules and Work Outline for Moral Education Directors and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools (Reported Yesterday) 154

Revised Work Outline for Moral Education Directors and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools (Promulgated by the Central Mass Movement Guidance Committee before August 16, 1935, and revised by the Mass Training Department of the Fifth Central Executive Committee on March 1, 1936) (Work Common to Moral Education Directors and Civic Education Teachers) A. Regarding Assisting School Administration: 1. Assist the principal in implementing laws and plans related to Party ideology education; 2. Assist the principal in enriching the implementation of Party ideology education; 3. Discuss and consult with the principal to formulate moral education programs; 4. Discuss and consult with the principal to prepare a work implementation plan at the beginning of each semester and submit it to the competent educational administrative agency for forwarding to the Moral Education Director and Civic Education Teacher Qualification Review Committee for record. B. Regarding Guiding Student Life: 1. At the weekly memorial service for the Premier, various commemorative events, and various gatherings, give speeches appropriate to the occasion on the Premier's will, revolutionary history, the crimes of the Communists, and the course of national disasters, and report on current affairs in accordance with the central government's policies; 2. Guide and encourage students to participate in extracurricular activities so that Party ideology education can permeate all aspects of student life; 3. Investigate the publications read by students and the types of friends they make, as well as their usual words and actions, in order to detect their attitude towards the Party and their thoughts and lives; 4. Use various suggestive methods to alert students in order to cultivate their national consciousness and patriotic concepts; 5. Actually participate in student group meetings and activities in order to achieve the effect of guidance and practice. C. Regarding Self-Cultivation: 1. Thoroughly study the Premier's will and the important declarations and resolutions of the Party, and read more of the speeches and writings of the Party's pioneers; 2. Love the Party and the country, encourage moral character, practice the New Life Movement, and be a role model for students; 3. Pay attention to studying the following items: 1. The current educational policy of our country; 2. Youth psychology, mental health, and mass psychology; 3. International and domestic current affairs. Work of the Moral Education Director: A. Execution Matters: 1. Execute laws and regulations related to moral education; 2. Execute the resolutions of the moral education conference and the moral education guidance committee regarding moral education; 3. Execute matters assigned by the principal. B. Planning Matters: 1. Formulate moral education implementation measures based on the moral education program; 2. Formulate student conduct examination measures; 3. Formulate student reward and punishment measures; 4. Plan methods for liaison between the school, the family, and society; 5. Formulate public covenants for classrooms, dormitories, dining halls, study rooms, etc.; 6. Formulate other plans and forms related to moral education. C. Guidance Matters: 1. Live with students and practice personality edification; 2. Guide students' daily life matters and promote the New Life Movement; 3. Handle disputes and other sudden events among students; 4. Guide students in serving the community; 5. Guide students in labor practice; 6. Investigate students' thoughts, personalities, and family circumstances; 7. Examine students' requests for leave, truancy, and absence from the Premier's Memorial Week and various gatherings; 8. Examine the effectiveness of moral education implementation; 9. Other. D. Advanced Studies: 1. Exploration of moral education theory; 2. Research on moral education implementation methods. Work of the Civic Education Teacher: A. Planning Matters: 1. Formulate civic education teaching programs; 2. Formulate civic training implementation measures based on the moral education program; 3. Plan methods for guiding student thinking; 4. Formulate other plans and forms necessary for teaching. B. Guidance Matters: 1. Lead students on field trips; 2. Examine students' reactions to civic education. C. Advanced Studies: 1. Research on civic courses and teaching methods; 2. Research on issues related to civic training. Matters to be Noted: 1. Moral education directors and civic education teachers should contact each other and assist each other; 2. Moral education directors and civic education teachers should find ways to contact all school staff and teachers (pay attention to military instructors, Boy Scout leaders, and physical education teachers) to implement Party ideology education consistently; 3. The teaching materials for civic education, Chinese, history, geography, and other subjects should strive for continuity.

Measures for Assessing the Work Performance of Moral Education Directors and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools (Promulgated by the Mass Training Department of the Fifth Central Executive Committee on March 1, 1936) 1. The work performance of moral education directors and civic education teachers (hereinafter referred to as "public education personnel") in secondary schools in each province and city shall be assessed by the Moral Education Director and Civic Education Teacher Qualification Review Committee (hereinafter referred to as the "Review Committee") in each locality in accordance with these measures. 2. The scope of the work performance assessment of public education personnel shall be the work stipulated in the Work Outline for Moral Education Directors and Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools, and shall be assessed separately. 3. The methods for assessing the work performance of public education personnel are divided into the following two types: A. The Review Committee in each province and city shall print and issue the "Work Report Form for Moral Education Directors in Secondary Schools" and the "Work Report Form for Civic Education Teachers in Secondary Schools" in accordance with the format prescribed by the central government to the highest educational administrative agency in the locality, and instruct the principals of each secondary school to fill them out in detail at the end of each semester for assessment. B. The Review Committee in each province and city may, in conjunction with the highest educational administrative agency in the locality, send personnel to conduct on-site observations. 4. The Review Committee in each province and city shall report the assessment results of the previous semester to the Central Mass Training Department before the start of each semester. 5. These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Central Mass Training Department. (End)

Ni Daoxiu Returns Home After Completing His Studies 160

Ni Jun Daoxiu, Jin Shan Lai, graduated from the Department of Electrical Engineering of the College of Engineering of National Zhejiang University in the autumn of 1931. With the financial assistance of his adoptive father, Gan Wangshan, he went to Germany at his own expense in October of the same year for an internship. He successively entered Berlin AEG and Siemens factories for two years. At the same time, he also entered the University of Berlin to study theory, so that theory and practice were not neglected. Therefore, in Germany, all grades were considered excellent. However, Ni Jun's desire for knowledge has not diminished. In the spring of 1934, he transferred to London, England, and entered the Maowei and Cale Company for a two-year internship. His grades were the best among his peers. It is heard that Mr. Ni has now been hired by the Shanghai Cale Branch and has left England for the United States. He changed to President Qin Ke Xun in Seattle, USA, at the beginning of this month and will arrive in Shanghai on the 17th of this month.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (2)(0)(2) 163

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

When a song was over, Ned bowed and wanted to retreat, but others would not let him go. They clapped non-stop, forcing him to come back again. When he came back again, he had a happy look on his face, and others felt happy when they saw it, because he did his best to give them cheerful old tunes, so that their feet also heard and danced, and everyone had moved and could not be quiet again.

"Quickly clear the deck!" Amy shouted: In less than a minute, the chairs had all been pushed to the back, the elderly were settled in the corners, and the children gathered on the stage.

"Be polite!" Amy shouted again: So the children all jumped to the women, and politely asked them to dance, regardless of the young or old. The little boys almost used force to grab the golden curls, but she chose Dick with a compassionate heart, letting him proudly lead her over. Xu Quren was also not allowed not to join: Aunt Amy gave Donn indescribable pleasure, because she resigned from Fulan and was willing to be with him. Naturally, Nann and Tomo, Ned and Xiao Mei each formed a pair, while Uncle Tandy invited Yaxi, who had been eager to try, and now suddenly felt flattered to receive such glory. Mr. Lai and An Manli danced alone in the doorway, and Mei Zhuang was really happy in half an hour.
